class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Arran</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="/\xc3\xa6/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">\xc3\xa6</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/\xc9\x99n/: &#39;on&#39; in &#39;button&#39;">\xc9\x99n</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Gaelic language">Scottish Gaelic</a>: <i lang="gd">Eilean Arainn</i> <small>pronounced&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Help:IPA/Scottish Gaelic">[elan \xcb\x88ar\xc9\xaa\xc9\xb2]</a></span>) or the <b>Isle of Arran</b> is an island off the coast of Scotland, in the United Kingdom. It is the largest island in the <a href="/wiki/Firth_of_Clyde" title="Firth of Clyde">Firth of Clyde</a> and the seventh largest Scottish island, at 432 square kilometres (167&#160;sq&#160;mi). <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Counties of Scotland">Historically</a> part of <a href="/wiki/Buteshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Buteshire">Buteshire</a>, it is in the <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_Scotland" title="Subdivisions of Scotland">unitary council area</a> of <a href="/wiki/North_Ayrshire" title="North Ayrshire">North Ayrshire</a>. In the 2011 census it had a resident population of 4,629. Though culturally and physically similar to the <a href="/wiki/Hebrides" title="Hebrides">Hebrides</a>, it is separated from them by the <a href="/wiki/Kintyre" title="Kintyre">Kintyre</a> peninsula. Often referred to as "Scotland in miniature", the island is divided into highland and lowland areas by the <a href="/wiki/Highland_Boundary_Fault" title="Highland Boundary Fault">Highland Boundary Fault</a> and has been described as a "geologist\'s paradise".<sup id="cite_ref-HSmith_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HSmith-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Arran has been continuously inhabited since the early <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> period. Numerous <a href="/wiki/Prehistory" title="Prehistory">prehistoric</a> remains have been found. From the 6th century onwards, <a href="/wiki/Goidelic_languages" title="Goidelic languages">Goidelic-speaking</a> peoples from Ireland colonised it and it became a centre of religious activity. In the troubled <a href="/wiki/Viking_Age" title="Viking Age">Viking Age</a>, Arran became the property of the <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norwegian</a> crown, until formally absorbed by the kingdom of Scotland in the 13th century. The 19th-century "<a href="/wiki/Clearances" class="mw-redirect" title="Clearances">clearances</a>" led to significant depopulation and the end of the Gaelic language and way of life. The economy and population have recovered in recent years, the main industry being tourism. There is a diversity of wildlife, including three species of tree <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> to the area.\n</p><p>The island includes miles of coastal pathways, numerous hills and mountains, forested areas, rivers, small lochs and beaches. Its main beaches are at <a href="/wiki/Brodick" title="Brodick">Brodick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whiting_Bay" title="Whiting Bay">Whiting Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kildonan,_Arran" title="Kildonan, Arran">Kildonan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sannox" title="Sannox">Sannox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Blackwaterfoot" title="Blackwaterfoot">Blackwaterfoot</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctext">Etymology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Geography"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Geography</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Villages"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Villages</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Surrounding_islands"><span class="tocnumber">2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Surrounding islands</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#Geology"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Geology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Climate"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Climate</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#Prehistory"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Prehistory</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Gaels,_Vikings_and_Middle_Ages"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Gaels, Vikings and Middle Ages</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Modern_era"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Modern era</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Gaelic"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Gaelic</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Local_government"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Local government</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Health_services"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Health services</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Transport"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Transport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Tourism"><span class="tocnumber">10.1</span> <span class="toctext">Tourism</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Other_industries"><span class="tocnumber">10.2</span> <span class="toctext">Other industries</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Nature_and_conservation"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Nature and conservation</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#North_Arran_National_Scenic_Area"><span class="tocnumber">12.1</span> <span class="toctext">North Arran National Scenic Area</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Notable_residents"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Notable residents</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Most of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Scotland" title="List of islands of Scotland">islands of Scotland</a> have been occupied consecutively by speakers of at least four languages since the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a>. Many of the names of these islands have more than one possible meaning as a result. Arran is therefore not unusual in that the derivation of the name is far from clear. Mac an T\xc3\xa0illeir (2003) states that "it is said to be unrelated to the name <a href="/wiki/Aran_Islands" title="Aran Islands">Aran</a> in Ireland" (which means "kidney-shaped", cf Irish <i>\xc3\xa1ra</i> "kidney").<sup id="cite_ref-MacanT2_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacanT2-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Unusually for a Scottish island, Haswell-Smith (2004) offers a <a href="/wiki/British_language_(Celtic)" class="mw-redirect" title="British language (Celtic)">Brythonic</a> derivation and a meaning of "high place" which at least corresponds with the geography \xe2\x80\x94 Arran is significantly loftier than all the land that immediately surrounds it along the shores of the Firth of Clyde.<sup id="cite_ref-HSmith_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HSmith-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Any other <a href="/wiki/Brythonic_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Brythonic languages">Brythonic</a> place-names that may have existed were later replaced on Arran as the Goidelic-speaking <a href="/wiki/Gaels" title="Gaels">Gaels</a> spread from Ireland, via their adjacent kingdom of <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1l_Riata" title="D\xc3\xa1l Riata">D\xc3\xa1l Riata</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Viking_Age" title="Viking Age">Viking Age</a> it became, along with most Scottish islands, the property of the <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norwegian</a> crown, at which time it may have been known as "Herrey" or "Hersey". As a result of this <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Norse</a> influence, many current place-names on Arran are of Viking origin.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cir_Mhor_and_Caisteal_Abhail.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Cir_Mhor_and_Caisteal_Abhail.JPG/220px-Cir_Mhor_and_Caisteal_Abhail.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Cir_Mhor_and_Caisteal_Abhail.JPG/330px-Cir_Mhor_and_Caisteal_Abhail.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Cir_Mhor_and_Caisteal_Abhail.JPG/440px-Cir_Mhor_and_Caisteal_Abhail.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cir_Mhor_and_Caisteal_Abhail.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/C%C3%ACr_Mh%C3%B2r" title="C\xc3\xacr Mh\xc3\xb2r">C\xc3\xacr Mh\xc3\xb2r</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caisteal_Abhail" title="Caisteal Abhail">Caisteal Abhail</a> seen from North Goatfell</div></div></div>\n<p>The island lies in the <a href="/wiki/Firth_of_Clyde" title="Firth of Clyde">Firth of Clyde</a> between <a href="/wiki/Ayr" title="Ayr">Ayr</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ardrossan" title="Ardrossan">Ardrossan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kintyre" title="Kintyre">Kintyre</a>. The profile of the north Arran hills as seen from the <a href="/wiki/Ayrshire" title="Ayrshire">Ayrshire</a> coast is referred to as the "<a href="/wiki/Sleeping_Warrior" title="Sleeping Warrior">Sleeping Warrior</a>", due to its resemblance to a resting human figure.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The highest of these hills is <a href="/wiki/Goat_Fell" title="Goat Fell">Goat Fell</a> at 873.5 metres (2,866&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> There are three other <a href="/wiki/Corbett_(mountain)" class="mw-redirect" title="Corbett (mountain)">Corbetts</a>, all in the north east: <a href="/wiki/Caisteal_Abhail" title="Caisteal Abhail">Caisteal Abhail</a>, <a href="/wiki/C%C3%ACr_Mh%C3%B2r" title="C\xc3\xacr Mh\xc3\xb2r">C\xc3\xacr Mh\xc3\xb2r</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beinn_Tarsuinn_(Corbett)" title="Beinn Tarsuinn (Corbett)">Beinn Tarsuinn</a>. Beinn Bharrain is the highest peak in the north west at 721 metres (2,365&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The largest glen on the island is Glen Iorsa to the west, whilst narrow Glen Sannox (<a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Gaelic</a>: <i>Gleann Shannaig</i>) and Glen Rosa (<a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Gaelic</a>: <i>Gleann R\xc3\xb2sa</i>) to the east surround Goat Fell. The terrain to the south is less mountainous, although a considerable portion of the interior lies above 350 metres (1,150&#160;ft), and A\' Chruach reaches 512 metres (1,680&#160;ft) at its summit.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OS_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OS-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> There are two other <a href="/wiki/Marilyn_(hill)" class="mw-redirect" title="Marilyn (hill)">Marilyns</a> in the south, <a href="/wiki/Tighvein" title="Tighvein">Tighvein</a> and Mullach M\xc3\xb2r (Holy Isle).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Villages">Villages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Villages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Villages_in_the_Isle_of_Arran" title="Category:Villages in the Isle of Arran">Category:Villages in the Isle of Arran</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lochranza.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Lochranza.jpg/220px-Lochranza.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Lochranza.jpg/330px-Lochranza.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Lochranza.jpg/440px-Lochranza.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="401" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lochranza.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lochranza" title="Lochranza">Lochranza</a> village and <a href="/wiki/Lochranza_Castle" title="Lochranza Castle">castle</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Holy_Isle_from_Lamlash.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Holy_Isle_from_Lamlash.jpg/220px-Holy_Isle_from_Lamlash.jpg" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Holy_Isle_from_Lamlash.jpg/330px-Holy_Isle_from_Lamlash.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Holy_Isle_from_Lamlash.jpg/440px-Holy_Isle_from_Lamlash.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4091" data-file-height="2583" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Holy_Isle_from_Lamlash.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Holy_Isle,_Firth_of_Clyde" title="Holy Isle, Firth of Clyde">Holy Isle</a> as seen from Arran</div></div></div>\n<p>Arran has several villages, mainly around the shoreline. <a href="/wiki/Brodick" title="Brodick">Brodick</a> (<a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old Norse</a>: \'broad bay\') is the site of the ferry terminal, several hotels, and the majority of shops. <a href="/wiki/Brodick_Castle" title="Brodick Castle">Brodick Castle</a> is a seat of the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Hamilton" title="Duke of Hamilton">Dukes of Hamilton</a>. <a href="/wiki/Lamlash" title="Lamlash">Lamlash</a>, however, is the largest village on the island and in 2001 had a population of 1,010 compared to 621 for Brodick.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Other villages include <a href="/wiki/Lochranza" title="Lochranza">Lochranza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catacol" title="Catacol">Catacol</a> in the north, <a href="/wiki/Corrie,_Arran" title="Corrie, Arran">Corrie</a> in the north east, <a href="/wiki/Blackwaterfoot" title="Blackwaterfoot">Blackwaterfoot</a> in the south west, <a href="/wiki/Kildonan,_Arran" title="Kildonan, Arran">Kildonan</a> in the south and <a href="/wiki/Whiting_Bay" title="Whiting Bay">Whiting Bay</a> in the south east.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Surrounding_islands">Surrounding islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Surrounding islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Islands_of_the_Clyde" title="Islands of the Clyde">Islands of the Clyde</a></div>\n<p>Arran has three smaller satellite islands: <a href="/wiki/Holy_Isle,_Firth_of_Clyde" title="Holy Isle, Firth of Clyde">Holy Isle</a> lies to the east opposite Lamlash, <a href="/wiki/Pladda" title="Pladda">Pladda</a> is located off Arran\'s south coast and tiny Hamilton Isle lies just off Clauchlands Point 1.2 kilometres (0.75&#160;mi) north of Holy Isle. Eilean na h-\xc3\x80irde B\xc3\xa0ine off the south west of Arran at Corriecravie is a <a href="/wiki/Skerry" title="Skerry">skerry</a> connected to Arran at low tide.\n</p><p>Other islands in the <a href="/wiki/Firth_of_Clyde" title="Firth of Clyde">Firth of Clyde</a> include <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Bute" title="Isle of Bute">Bute</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Cumbrae" title="Great Cumbrae">Great Cumbrae</a> and <a href="/wiki/Inchmarnock" title="Inchmarnock">Inchmarnock</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The division between the "Highland" and "Lowland" areas of Arran is marked by the <a href="/wiki/Highland_Boundary_Fault" title="Highland Boundary Fault">Highland Boundary Fault</a> which runs north east to south west across Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-McK300_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McK300-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Arran is a popular destination for <a href="/wiki/Geologist" title="Geologist">geologists</a>, who come to see <a href="/wiki/Igneous_rock" title="Igneous rock">intrusive igneous landforms</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Sill_(geology)" title="Sill (geology)">sills</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dike_(geology)" title="Dike (geology)">dykes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sedimentary" class="mw-redirect" title="Sedimentary">sedimentary</a> and meta-sedimentary rocks ranging in age from <a href="/wiki/Precambrian" title="Precambrian">Precambrian</a> to <a href="/wiki/Mesozoic" title="Mesozoic">Mesozoic</a>.\n</p><p>Most of the interior of the northern half of the island is taken up by a large <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a> <a href="/wiki/Batholith" title="Batholith">batholith</a> that was created by substantial magmatic activity around 58 million years ago in the <a href="/wiki/Paleogene" title="Paleogene">Paleogene</a> period.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> This comprises an outer ring of coarse granite and an inner core of finer grained granite, which was intruded later. This granite was intruded into the Late <a href="/wiki/Proterozoic" title="Proterozoic">Proterozoic</a> to Cambrian metasediments of the <a href="/wiki/Dalradian" title="Dalradian">Dalradian</a> Supergroup. Other Paleogene igneous rocks on Arran include extensive <a href="/wiki/Felsic" title="Felsic">felsic</a> and composite sills in the south of the island, and the central ring complex, an eroded caldera system surrounded by a near-continuous ring of granitic rocks.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sedimentary rocks dominate the southern half of the island, especially <a href="/wiki/Old_Red_Sandstone" title="Old Red Sandstone">Old</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Red_Sandstone" title="New Red Sandstone">New Red Sandstone</a>. Some of these sandstones contain <a href="/wiki/Fulgurite" title="Fulgurite">fulgurites</a> \xe2\x80\x93 pitted marks that may have been created by Permian lightning strikes.<sup id="cite_ref-McK300_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McK300-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Large <a href="/wiki/Aeolian_processes" title="Aeolian processes">aeolian</a> sand dunes are preserved in <a href="/wiki/Permian" title="Permian">Permian</a> sandstones near <a href="/wiki/Brodick" title="Brodick">Brodick</a>, showing the presence of an ancient desert. Within the central complex are subsided blocks of Triassic sandstone and <a href="/wiki/Marl" title="Marl">marl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jurassic" title="Jurassic">Jurassic</a> shale, and even a rare example of <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">Cretaceous</a> chalk.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> During the 19th century <a href="/wiki/Baryte" title="Baryte">barytes</a> was mined near <a href="/wiki/Sannox" title="Sannox">Sannox</a>. First discovered in 1840, nearly 5,000 tons were produced between 1853 and 1862. The mine was closed by the <a href="/wiki/William_Hamilton,_11th_Duke_of_Hamilton" title="William Hamilton, 11th Duke of Hamilton">11th Duke of Hamilton</a> on the grounds that it "spoiled the solemn grandeur of the scene" but was reopened after the First World War and operated until 1938 when the vein ran out.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Visiting in 1787, the geologist <a href="/wiki/James_Hutton" title="James Hutton">James Hutton</a> found his first example of an <a href="/wiki/Hutton%27s_Unconformity" title="Hutton&#39;s Unconformity">unconformity</a> to the north of Newton Point near <a href="/wiki/Lochranza" title="Lochranza">Lochranza</a>, which provided evidence for his <a href="/wiki/Plutonism" title="Plutonism">Plutonist</a> theories of <a href="/wiki/Uniformitarianism_(science)" class="mw-redirect" title="Uniformitarianism (science)">uniformitarianism</a> and about the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_the_Earth" title="Age of the Earth">age of the Earth</a>. This spot is one of the most famous places in the study of geology.<sup id="cite_ref-monty_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-monty-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Waymarking_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Waymarking-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a> glaciations almost entirely covered Scotland in ice, and Arran\'s highest peaks may have been <a href="/wiki/Nunatak" title="Nunatak">nunataks</a> at this time.<sup id="cite_ref-McK300_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McK300-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> After the last retreat of the ice at the close of the <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a> epoch <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea levels</a> were up to 70 metres (230&#160;ft) lower than at present and it is likely that circa 14,000 <a href="/wiki/Before_Present" title="Before Present">BP</a> the island was connected to mainland Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Sea level changes and the <a href="/wiki/Isostasy" title="Isostasy">isostatic</a> rise of land makes charting <a href="/wiki/Post-glacial" class="mw-redirect" title="Post-glacial">post-glacial</a> coastlines a complex task, but it is evident that the island is ringed by <a href="/wiki/Quaternary_glaciation" title="Quaternary glaciation">post glacial</a> <a href="/wiki/Raised_beach" title="Raised beach">raised beaches</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Cave" title="King&#39;s Cave">King\'s Cave</a> on the south west coast is an example of an <a href="/wiki/Emergent_coastline" title="Emergent coastline">emergent landform</a> on such a raised beach. This cave, which is over 30.5 metres (100&#160;ft) long and up to 15.3 metres (50&#160;ft) high, lies well above the present day sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> There are tall sea cliffs to the north east including large rock slides under the heights of Torr Reamhar, <a href="/wiki/Torr_Meadhonach" title="Torr Meadhonach">Torr Meadhonach</a> and at Scriden (<i>An Scriodan</i>) at the far north end of the island.<sup id="cite_ref-OS_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OS-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The influence of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a> create a mild oceanic climate. Temperatures are generally cool, averaging about 6&#160;<a href="/wiki/Celsius" title="Celsius">\xc2\xb0C</a> (43&#160;<a href="/wiki/Fahrenheit" title="Fahrenheit">\xc2\xb0F</a>) in January and 16&#160;\xc2\xb0C (61&#160;\xc2\xb0F) in July at sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-met_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-met-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The southern half of the island, being less mountainous, has a more favourable climate than the north, and the east coast is more sheltered from the prevailing winds than the west and south.\n</p><p>Snow seldom lies at sea level and frosts are less frequent than on the mainland. As in most islands of the west coast of Scotland, annual rainfall is generally high at between 1,500&#160;mm (59&#160;in) in the south and west and 1,900&#160;mm (75&#160;in) in the north and east. The mountains are wetter still with the summits receiving over 2,550&#160;mm (100&#160;in) annually. May and June are the sunniest months, with upwards of 200 hours of bright sunshine being recorded on average.<sup id="cite_ref-met_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-met-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MachrieMoorStones.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/MachrieMoorStones.jpg/220px-MachrieMoorStones.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/MachrieMoorStones.jpg/330px-MachrieMoorStones.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/MachrieMoorStones.jpg/440px-MachrieMoorStones.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="429" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MachrieMoorStones.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Machrie Moor Standing Stones</div></div></div>\n<p>Arran has a particular concentration of early <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> <a href="/wiki/Chambered_cairn#Clyde-Carlingford" title="Chambered cairn">Clyde Cairns</a>, a form of <a href="/wiki/Gallery_grave" title="Gallery grave">Gallery grave</a>. The typical style of these is a rectangular or trapezoidal stone and earth mound that encloses a chamber lined with larger stone slabs. Pottery and bone fragments found inside them suggest they were used for interment and some have forecourts, which may have been an area for public display or ritual. There are two good examples in Monamore Glen west of the village of Lamlash,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> and similar structures called the <a href="/wiki/Giants%27_Graves,_Arran" title="Giants&#39; Graves, Arran">Giants\' Graves</a> above Whiting Bay. There are numerous standing stones dating from prehistoric times, including six stone circles on <a href="/wiki/Machrie_Moor_Stone_Circles" title="Machrie Moor Stone Circles">Machrie Moor</a> (Gaelic: <i>Am Machaire</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Pitchstone" title="Pitchstone">Pitchstone</a> deposits on the island were used locally for making various items in the <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a> era.<sup id="cite_ref-ballin_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ballin-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Early_Bronze_Age" class="mw-redirect" title="Early Bronze Age">Early Bronze Age</a> pitchstone from the Isle of Arran or items made from it were transported around Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-ballin_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ballin-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Several <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> sites have been excavated, including Ossian\'s Mound near Clachaig and a cairn near Blackwaterfoot that produced a bronze dagger and a gold fillet.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Torr a\' Chaisteal Dun in the south west near Sliddery is the ruin of an <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> fortified structure dating from about AD 200. The original walls would have been 3 metres (9.8&#160;ft) or more thick and enclosed a circular area about 14 metres (46&#160;ft) in diameter.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Gaels.2C_Vikings_and_Middle_Ages"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Gaels,_Vikings_and_Middle_Ages">Gaels, Vikings and Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Gaels, Vikings and Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lochranza_castle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Lochranza_castle.jpg/220px-Lochranza_castle.jpg" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Lochranza_castle.jpg/330px-Lochranza_castle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Lochranza_castle.jpg/440px-Lochranza_castle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="552" data-file-height="383" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lochranza_castle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lochranza_Castle" title="Lochranza Castle">Lochranza Castle</a></div></div></div>\n<p>An ancient Irish poem called <i>Agalllamh na Senorach</i>, first recorded in the 13th century, describes the attractions of the island.\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><div class="poem">\n<p>Arran of the many stags<br />\nThe sea strikes against her shoulders,<br />\nCompanies of men can feed there,<br />\nBlue spears are reddened among her boulders.<br />\n<br />\nMerry hinds are on her hills,<br />\nJuicy berries are there for food,<br />\nRefreshing water in her streams,<br />\nNuts in plenty in the wood.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n<p>The monastery of <i>Aileach</i> founded by <a href="/wiki/Brendan" title="Brendan">St. Brendan</a> in the 6th century may have been on Arran and <a href="/wiki/Molaise_of_Leighlin" title="Molaise of Leighlin">St. Molaise</a> was also active, with Holy Isle being a centre of Brendan\'s activities.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The caves below Keil Point (<a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Gaelic</a>: <i>Rubha na Cille</i>) contain a slab which may have been an ancient altar. This stone has two <a href="/wiki/Petrosomatoglyph" title="Petrosomatoglyph">petrosomatoglyphs</a> on it, the prints of two right feet, said to be of Saint Columba.<sup id="cite_ref-Beare_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beare-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cliffs_at_Blackwaterfoot,_Arran.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Cliffs_at_Blackwaterfoot%2C_Arran.JPG/220px-Cliffs_at_Blackwaterfoot%2C_Arran.JPG" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Cliffs_at_Blackwaterfoot%2C_Arran.JPG/330px-Cliffs_at_Blackwaterfoot%2C_Arran.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Cliffs_at_Blackwaterfoot%2C_Arran.JPG/440px-Cliffs_at_Blackwaterfoot%2C_Arran.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2498" data-file-height="1624" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cliffs_at_Blackwaterfoot,_Arran.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cliffs at Blackwaterfoot</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%27King%27s_Cave%27,_Arran.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/%27King%27s_Cave%27%2C_Arran.JPG/220px-%27King%27s_Cave%27%2C_Arran.JPG" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/%27King%27s_Cave%27%2C_Arran.JPG/330px-%27King%27s_Cave%27%2C_Arran.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/%27King%27s_Cave%27%2C_Arran.JPG/440px-%27King%27s_Cave%27%2C_Arran.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2523" data-file-height="1695" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%27King%27s_Cave%27,_Arran.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The "King\'s Cave", reputedly a refuge of King Robert the Bruce</div></div></div>\n<p>In the 11th century Arran became part of the Sodor (Old Norse: \'Su\xc3\xb0r-eyjar\'), or South Isles of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Mann_and_the_Isles" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Mann and the Isles">Kingdom of Mann and the Isles</a>, but on the death of <a href="/wiki/Godred_Crovan" title="Godred Crovan">Godred Crovan</a> in 1095 all the isles came under the direct rule of <a href="/wiki/Magnus_III_of_Norway" class="mw-redirect" title="Magnus III of Norway">Magnus III of Norway</a>. <a href="/wiki/L%C7%ABgma%C3%B0r_Gu%C3%B0r%C3%B8%C3%B0arson" title="L\xc7\xabgma\xc3\xb0r Gu\xc3\xb0r\xc3\xb8\xc3\xb0arson">Lagman</a> (1103\xe2\x80\x931104) restored local rule. After the death of <a href="/wiki/Somerled" title="Somerled">Somerled</a> in 1164, Arran and Bute were ruled by his son Angus.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In 1237, the Scottish isles broke away completely from the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a> and became an independent kingdom. After the indecisive <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Largs" title="Battle of Largs">Battle of Largs</a> between the kingdoms of Norway and Scotland in 1263, <a href="/wiki/Haakon_IV_of_Norway" title="Haakon IV of Norway">Haakon Haakonsson, King of Norway</a> reclaimed Norwegian lordship over the "provinces" of the west. Arriving at <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Mull" class="mw-redirect" title="Isle of Mull">Mull</a>, he rewarded a number of his Norse-Gaelic vassals with grants of lands. Bute was given to <a href="/wiki/Ruadhri_of_Bute" title="Ruadhri of Bute">Ruadhri</a> and Arran to Murchad MacSween.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;Note 1&#93;</a></sup> Following Haakon\'s death later that year Norway ceded the islands of western Scotland to the Scottish crown in 1266 by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Perth" title="Treaty of Perth">Treaty of Perth</a>. A substantial Viking grave has been discovered near King\'s Cross south of Lamlash, containing whalebone, iron rivets and nails, fragments of <a href="/wiki/Bronze" title="Bronze">bronze</a> and a 9th-century bronze coin, and another grave of similar date nearby yielded a sword and shield.<sup id="cite_ref-Haco_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haco-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Arran was also part of the medieval <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Sodor_and_Man" title="Bishop of Sodor and Man">Bishopric of Sodor and Man</a>.\n</p><p>On the opposite side of the island near Blackwaterfoot is the King\'s Cave (see above), where <a href="/wiki/Robert_the_Bruce" title="Robert the Bruce">Robert the Bruce</a> is said to have taken shelter in the 14th century.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Bruce returned to the island in 1326, having earlier granted lands to Fergus MacLouis for assistance rendered during his time of concealment there. Brodick Castle played a prominent part in the island\'s medieval history. Probably dating from the 13th century, it was captured by English forces during the <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_Scottish_Independence" title="Wars of Scottish Independence">Wars of Independence</a> before being taken back by Scottish troops in 1307. It was badly damaged by action from English ships in 1406 and sustained an attack by <a href="/wiki/John_of_Islay,_Earl_of_Ross" title="John of Islay, Earl of Ross">John of Islay</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lord_of_the_Isles" title="Lord of the Isles">Lord of the Isles</a> in 1455. Originally a seat of the <a href="/wiki/Walter_Bailloch" title="Walter Bailloch">Clan Stewart of Menteith</a> it passed to the <a href="/wiki/Clan_Boyd" title="Clan Boyd">Boyd</a> family in the 15th century.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> For a short time during the reign of <a href="/wiki/King_James_V" class="mw-redirect" title="King James V">King James V</a> in the 16th century, the Isle of Arran was under the regency of <a href="/wiki/Robert_Maxwell,_5th_Lord_Maxwell" title="Robert Maxwell, 5th Lord Maxwell">Robert Maxwell, 5th Lord Maxwell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_era">Modern era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Modern era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scotland,_Isle_of_Arran,_Lamlash,_Hamilton_Terrace.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Scotland%2C_Isle_of_Arran%2C_Lamlash%2C_Hamilton_Terrace.JPG/220px-Scotland%2C_Isle_of_Arran%2C_Lamlash%2C_Hamilton_Terrace.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Scotland%2C_Isle_of_Arran%2C_Lamlash%2C_Hamilton_Terrace.JPG/330px-Scotland%2C_Isle_of_Arran%2C_Lamlash%2C_Hamilton_Terrace.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Scotland%2C_Isle_of_Arran%2C_Lamlash%2C_Hamilton_Terrace.JPG/440px-Scotland%2C_Isle_of_Arran%2C_Lamlash%2C_Hamilton_Terrace.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1716" data-file-height="1140" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scotland,_Isle_of_Arran,_Lamlash,_Hamilton_Terrace.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"Hamilton Terrace" with the Clearances Monument, Lamlash</div></div></div>\n<p>At the commencement of the <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">Early modern period</a> <a href="/wiki/James_Hamilton,_1st_Earl_of_Arran" title="James Hamilton, 1st Earl of Arran">James, 2nd Lord Hamilton</a> became a <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_of_Scotland" title="Privy Council of Scotland">privy counsellor</a> to his first cousin, <a href="/wiki/James_IV_of_Scotland" title="James IV of Scotland">James IV of Scotland</a> and helped to arrange his marriage to Princess <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Tudor" title="Margaret Tudor">Margaret Tudor</a> of England. As a reward he was created Earl of Arran in 1503. The local economy for much of this period was based on the <a href="/wiki/Run_rig" title="Run rig">run rig</a> system, the basic crops being oats, barley and potatoes. The population slowly grew to about 6,500. In the early 19th century <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Douglas-Hamilton,_10th_Duke_of_Hamilton" class="mw-redirect" title="Alexander Douglas-Hamilton, 10th Duke of Hamilton">Alexander, 10th Duke of Hamilton</a> (1767\xe2\x80\x931852) embarked on a programme of <a href="/wiki/Highland_Clearances" title="Highland Clearances">clearances</a> that had a devastating effect on the island\'s population. These "improvements" typically led to land that had been rented out to as many as 27 families being converted into a single farm. In some cases, land was promised in Canada for each adult emigrant male. In April 1829, for example, 86 islanders boarded the brig <i>Caledonia</i> for the two-month journey, half their fares being paid for by the Duke. However, on arrival in <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> only 41 hectares (100 acres) was made available to the heads of extended families. Whole villages were removed and the Gaelic culture of the island devastated. The writer <a href="/wiki/James_Hogg" title="James Hogg">James Hogg</a> wrote, "Ah! Wae\'s [Woe is] me. I hear the Duke of Hamilton\'s crofters are a\'gaun away, man and mother\'s son, frae the Isle o\' Arran. Pity on us!".<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> A memorial to this has been constructed on the shore at Lamlash, paid for by a Canadian descendant of the emigrants.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 10 August 1941 a RAF <a href="/wiki/Preproduction_B-24" class="mw-redirect" title="Preproduction B-24">Consolidated B-24 Liberator LB-30A</a> AM261 was flying from <a href="/wiki/RAF_Heathfield" title="RAF Heathfield">RAF Heathfield</a> in Ayrshire to <a href="/wiki/Gander_International_Airport" title="Gander International Airport">Gander International Airport</a> in Canada. However, the B-24 crashed into the hillside of Mullach Buidhe north of Goat Fell, killing all 22 passengers and crew.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin: auto;">\n<caption>Overview of population trends\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<td><i><b>Year</b></i>\n</td>\n<td><i><b>Population</b></i><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><i><b>Year</b></i>\n</td>\n<td><i><b>Population</b></i>\n</td>\n<td rowspan="7"><a href="/wiki/File:Arran_population.svg" class="image"><img alt="Arran population.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Arran_population.svg/300px-Arran_population.svg.png" width="300" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Arran_population.svg/450px-Arran_population.svg.png 1.5x, /></a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1755\n</td>\n<td>3,646\n</td>\n<td>1931\n</td>\n<td>4,506\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1782\n</td>\n<td>5,804\n</td>\n<td>1961\n</td>\n<td>3,700\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1821\n</td>\n<td>6,600\n</td>\n<td>1971\n</td>\n<td>3,564\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1841\n</td>\n<td>6,241\n</td>\n<td>1981\n</td>\n<td>3,845\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1881\n</td>\n<td>4,730\n</td>\n<td>1991\n</td>\n<td>4,474\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1891\n</td>\n<td>4,824\n</td>\n<td>2001\n</td>\n<td>5,058\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>2011\n</td>\n<td>4,629\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Arran\'s resident population was 4,629 in 2011, a decline of just over 8 per cent from the 5,045 recorded in 2001,<sup id="cite_ref-census2001_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2001-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> against a background of Scottish island populations as a whole growing by 4 per cent to 103,702 over the same period.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gaelic">Gaelic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Gaelic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible collapsed">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="2" style="background:#efefef;">Pronunciation\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="vertical-align: top;">\n<td style="width: 40%;">\n</td>\n<th colspan="2" style="background:#efefef;">\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Scots_Gaelic" class="mw-redirect" title="Scots Gaelic">Scots Gaelic</a>:</td>\n<td>A\xe2\x80\x99 Chruach\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Pronunciation:</td>\n<td><small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"
