title="Scots Gaelic">Scots Gaelic</a>:</td>\n<td>Rubha na Cille\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Pronunciation:</td>\n<td><small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Help:IPA/Scottish Gaelic">[\xcb\x88r\xcb\xa0u.\xc9\x99 n\xc9\x99 \xcb\x88k\xca\xb2\xca\xb0i\xca\x8e\xc9\x99]</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Rubhanacille.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d3/Rubhanacille.ogg" class="internal" title="Rubhanacille.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Gaelic was still spoken widely on Arran at the beginning of the 20th century. The 1901 Census reported 25\xe2\x80\x9349 per cent Gaelic speakers on the eastern side of the island and 50\xe2\x80\x9374 per cent on the western side of the island. By 1921 the proportion for the whole island had dropped to less than 25 per cent.<sup id="cite_ref-MacT_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacT-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Nils_Holmer" title="Nils Holmer">Nils Holmer</a> quotes the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9illire" title="F\xc3\xa9illire">F\xc3\xa9illire</a> (a Gaelic <a href="/wiki/Almanack" class="mw-redirect" title="Almanack">almanack</a>) reporting 4,532 inhabitants on the island in 1931 with 605 Gaelic speakers, showing that Gaelic had declined to about 13 per cent of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-Holmer_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holmer-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> It continued to decline until the last native speakers of Arran Gaelic died in the 1990s. Current Gaelic speakers on Arran originate from other areas in Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, 2.0 per cent of Arran residents aged three and over could speak Gaelic.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Arran Gaelic is reasonably well documented. Holmer carried out field work on the island in 1938, reporting Gaelic being spoken by "a fair number of old inhabitants". He interviewed 53 informants from various locations and his description of <i>The Gaelic of Arran</i> was published in 1957 and runs to 211 pages of phonological, grammatical and lexical information. The <i>Survey of the Gaelic Dialects of Scotland</i>, which collected Gaelic dialect data in Scotland between 1950 and 1963, also interviewed five native speakers of Arran Gaelic.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Arran dialect falls firmly into the southern group of Gaelic dialects (referred to as the "peripheral" dialects in Celtic studies) and thus shows:<sup id="cite_ref-Holmer_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holmer-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>a <a href="/wiki/Glottal_stop" title="Glottal stop">glottal stop</a> replacing an <a href="/wiki/Old_Irish" title="Old Irish">Old Irish</a> <a href="/wiki/Hiatus_(linguistics)" title="Hiatus (linguistics)">hiatus</a>, e.g. <i>rathad</i> \'road\' <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/r\xc9\x9b\xca\x94\xc9\x99t\xcc\xaa/</span><sup id="cite_ref-Holmer_58-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holmer-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> (normally <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/r\xcb\xa0a.\xc9\x99t\xcc\xaa/</span>)</li>\n<li>the dropping of /h/ between vowels e.g. <i>athair</i> \'father\' <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/a\xc9\x99\xc9\xbe/</span><sup id="cite_ref-Holmer_58-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holmer-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> (normally <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ah\xc9\x99\xc9\xbe\xca\xb2/</span>)</li>\n<li>the preservation of a long l, n and r, e.g. <i>fann</i> \'weak\' <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/fan\xcc\xaa\xcb\xa0\xcb\x90/</span><sup id="cite_ref-Holmer_58-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holmer-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> (normally <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/faun\xcc\xaa\xcb\xa0/</span> with <a href="/wiki/Diphthong" title="Diphthong">diphthongisation</a>).</li></ul>\n<p>The most unusual feature of Arran Gaelic is the <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/w/</span> <a href="/wiki/Semivowel" title="Semivowel">glide</a> after <a href="/wiki/Labial_consonant" title="Labial consonant">labials</a> before a <a href="/wiki/Front_vowel" title="Front vowel">front vowel</a>, e.g. <i>maith</i> \'good\' <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/mw\xc9\x9bh/</span><sup id="cite_ref-Holmer_58-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holmer-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> (normally <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/mah/</span>).\n</p><p>Mac an T\xc3\xa0illeir notes that the island has a poetic name <i>Arainn nan Aighean Iomadh</i> - "Arran of the many stags" and that a native of the island or <i>Arainneach</i> is also nicknamed a <i>coinean m\xc3\xb2r</i> in Gaelic, meaning "big rabbit".<sup id="cite_ref-MacanT2_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacanT2-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Locally, <i>Arainn</i> was pronounced <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xc9\x9b\xc9\xbe\xc9\xaa\xc9\xb2/</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Holmer_58-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holmer-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">Local government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Local government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MapOfAyrshire.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/MapOfAyrshire.png/220px-MapOfAyrshire.png" width="220" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ea/MapOfAyrshire.png 1.5x" data-file-width="302" data-file-height="326" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MapOfAyrshire.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Arran\'s location within <a href="/wiki/Ayrshire" title="Ayrshire">Ayrshire</a></div></div></div>\n<p>From the 17th to the late 20th century, Arran was part of the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Bute" title="County of Bute">County of Bute</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> After the 1975 <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_(Scotland)_Act_1973" title="Local Government (Scotland) Act 1973">reorganisation of local government</a> Arran became part of the district of <a href="/wiki/Cunninghame" title="Cunninghame">Cunninghame</a> in <a href="/wiki/Strathclyde" title="Strathclyde">Strathclyde</a> Region.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> This two-tier system of local government lasted until 1996 when the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_etc._(Scotland)_Act_1994" title="Local Government etc. (Scotland) Act 1994">Local Government etc. (Scotland) Act 1994</a> came into effect, abolishing the regions and districts and replacing them with 32 <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_Scotland" title="Subdivisions of Scotland">council areas</a>. Arran is now in the <a href="/wiki/North_Ayrshire" title="North Ayrshire">North Ayrshire</a> council area, along with some of the other constituent islands of the County of Bute.\n</p><p>For some statistical purposes Arran is within the <a href="/wiki/Registration_county" title="Registration county">registration county</a> of <a href="/wiki/County_of_Bute" title="County of Bute">Bute</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> and for ceremonial purposes it forms part of the <a href="/wiki/Lieutenancy_areas_of_Scotland" title="Lieutenancy areas of Scotland">lieutenancy area</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ayrshire_and_Arran" title="Ayrshire and Arran">Ayrshire and Arran</a>.\n</p><p>In the House of Commons, since 2005 Arran has been part of <a href="/wiki/North_Ayrshire_and_Arran_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="North Ayrshire and Arran (UK Parliament constituency)">the Ayrshire North and Arran constituency</a>, represented since 2015 by <a href="/wiki/Patricia_Gibson" title="Patricia Gibson">Patricia Gibson</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">SNP</a>. It was previously part of the constituency of <a href="/wiki/Cunninghame_North_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Cunninghame North (UK Parliament constituency)">Cunninghame North</a> from 1983 to 2005, and of <a href="/wiki/Bute_and_North_Ayrshire_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bute and North Ayrshire (UK Parliament constituency)">Ayrshire North and Bute</a> from 1918 to 1983.\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a>, Arran is part of the constituency of <a href="/wiki/Cunninghame_North_(Scottish_Parliament_constituency)" title="Cunninghame North (Scottish Parliament constituency)">Cunninghame North</a>, currently represented by <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Gibson_(Scottish_politician)" title="Kenneth Gibson (Scottish politician)">Kenneth Gibson</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a> (SNP). The <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a> held the seat until 2007, when the SNP gained it with a majority of just 48, making it the most marginal seat in Holyrood until 2011, when the SNP significantly increased its majority to 6117 over Labour.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_services">Health services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Health services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><a href="/wiki/NHS_Ayrshire_and_Arran" title="NHS Ayrshire and Arran">NHS Ayrshire and Arran</a> is responsible for the provision of health services for the island. <a href="/wiki/Arran_War_Memorial_Hospital" title="Arran War Memorial Hospital">Arran War Memorial Hospital</a> is a 17-bed acute hospital at Lamlash. The Arran Medical Group provides primary-care services and supports the hospital. The practice is based at Brodick Health Centre and has three base surgeries and four branch surgeries.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Isle_of_Arran_OS_OpenData_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Isle_of_Arran_OS_OpenData_map.png/220px-Isle_of_Arran_OS_OpenData_map.png" width="220" height="309" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Isle_of_Arran_OS_OpenData_map.png/330px-Isle_of_Arran_OS_OpenData_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Isle_of_Arran_OS_OpenData_map.png/440px-Isle_of_Arran_OS_OpenData_map.png 2x" data-file-width="1008" data-file-height="1414" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Isle_of_Arran_OS_OpenData_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Arran. The island to the east is <a href="/wiki/Holy_Isle,_Firth_of_Clyde" title="Holy Isle, Firth of Clyde">Holy Isle</a> and the tiny island to the south is <a href="/wiki/Pladda" title="Pladda">Pladda</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Arran is connected to the Scottish mainland by two <a href="/wiki/Caledonian_MacBrayne" title="Caledonian MacBrayne">Caledonian MacBrayne</a> ferries; <a href="/wiki/MV_Caledonian_Isles" title="MV Caledonian Isles">MV&#160;<i>Caledonian Isles</i></a> from Brodick to Ardrossan, and <a href="/wiki/MV_Catriona" title="MV Catriona">MV&#160;<i>Catriona</i></a> (summer only) from Lochranza to <a href="/wiki/Claonaig" title="Claonaig">Claonaig</a>. The <a href="/wiki/MV_Isle_of_Arran" title="MV Isle of Arran">MV&#160;<i>Isle of Arran</i></a> provides additional summer sailings from Brodick to Ardrossan.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Summer day trips are also available on board the <a href="/wiki/Paddle_steamer" title="Paddle steamer">paddle steamer</a> <a href="/wiki/PS_Waverley" title="PS Waverley">PS&#160;<i>Waverley</i></a>, and a summer service operated by a local resident connects Lamlash to the neighbouring Holy Isle.\n</p><p>Brodick Ferry Terminal underwent \xc2\xa322 million of work to improve connections to the island. The new terminal includes better passenger facilities, increased passenger and freight capacity, and a new pier, all of which were set to open in August 2017 but finally opened on 20 March 2018, due to various construction issues. Additionally the island was due to be served by a new \xc2\xa345-million dual-fuelled ferry from 2018 \xe2\x80\x93 the <i><a href="/wiki/MV_Glen_Sannox_(2017)" title="MV Glen Sannox (2017)">MV Glen Sannox</a></i> \xe2\x80\x93 which will have a capacity of 1,000. This has also been delayed due to various construction issues and will not be available until late 2018 or early 2019.\n</p><p>There are three through roads on the island. The 90 kilometres (56&#160;mi) coast road circumnavigates the island. In 2007, a 48 kilometres (30&#160;mi) stretch of this road, previously designated as A841, was de-classified as a C road. Travelling south from Whiting Bay, the C147 goes round the south coast continuing north up the west coast of the island to Lochranza. At this point the road becomes the A841 down the east coast back to Whiting Bay.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> At one point the coast road ventures inland to climb the 200 metres (660&#160;ft) pass at the Boguillie between Creag Ghlas Laggan and Caisteal Abhail, located between Sannox and Lochranza.<sup id="cite_ref-OS_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OS-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The other two roads run across from the east to the west side of the island. The main cross-island road is the 19 kilometres (12&#160;mi) B880 from Brodick to Blackwaterfoot, called "The String", which climbs over Gleann an t-Suidhe. About 10 kilometres (6&#160;mi) from Brodick, a minor road branches off to the right to Machrie. The single-track road "The Ross" runs 15 kilometres (9&#160;mi) from Lamlash to Lagg and Sliddery via Glen Scorodale (<a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Gaelic</a>: <i>Gleann Sgoradail</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The island can be explored using a public bus service operated by <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_West_Scotland" title="Stagecoach West Scotland">Stagecoach</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The main bus terminal on the island is located in Brodick at the Ferry Terminal. The newly upgraded facility offers routes to all parts of the island.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PS_Waverley_off_Brodick_castle_1989.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/PS_Waverley_off_Brodick_castle_1989.jpg/220px-PS_Waverley_off_Brodick_castle_1989.jpg" width="220" height="96" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/PS_Waverley_off_Brodick_castle_1989.jpg/330px-PS_Waverley_off_Brodick_castle_1989.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/PS_Waverley_off_Brodick_castle_1989.jpg/440px-PS_Waverley_off_Brodick_castle_1989.jpg 2x" data-file-width="677" data-file-height="294" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PS_Waverley_off_Brodick_castle_1989.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/PS_Waverley" title="PS Waverley">PS <i>Waverley</i></a> in front of <a href="/wiki/Brodick_Castle" title="Brodick Castle">Brodick Castle</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The main industry on the island is tourism, with outdoor activities such as <a href="/wiki/Hiking" title="Hiking">walking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">cycling</a> and wildlife watching being especially popular.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Popular walking routes include climbing to the summit of <a href="/wiki/Goat_Fell" title="Goat Fell">Goat Fell</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Arran_Coastal_Way" title="Arran Coastal Way">Arran Coastal Way</a>, a 107 kilometre trail that goes around the coastline the island.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The Arran Coastal Way was designated as one of <a href="/wiki/Scotland%27s_Great_Trails" title="Scotland&#39;s Great Trails">Scotland\'s Great Trails</a> by <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Natural_Heritage" title="Scottish Natural Heritage">Scottish Natural Heritage</a> in June 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On of Arran\'s greatest attractions for tourists is <a href="/wiki/Brodick_Castle" title="Brodick Castle">Brodick Castle</a>, owned by the <a href="/wiki/National_Trust_for_Scotland" title="National Trust for Scotland">National Trust for Scotland</a>. The castle is currently closed to allow fire-safety and other conservation works to be undertaken, and will not re-open until 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Auchrannie Resort, which contains two hotels, three restaurants, two leisure complexes and an adventure company, is one of biggest employers on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Local businesses include the <a href="/wiki/Arran_Single_Malt" class="mw-redirect" title="Arran Single Malt">Arran Distillery</a>, which was opened in 1995 in <a href="/wiki/Lochranza" title="Lochranza">Lochranza</a>. This is open for tours and contains a shop and cafe. A second visitor centre has been announced for the south of the island, due to open in 2019. \n</p><p>The island has a number of golf courses including the 12 hole <a href="/wiki/Shiskine" title="Shiskine">Shiskine</a> <a href="/wiki/Links_(golf)" title="Links (golf)">links</a> course which was founded in 1896.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The village of <a href="/wiki/Lagg" title="Lagg">Lagg</a>, at the southern tip of Arran, has a <a href="/wiki/Naturism" title="Naturism">nudist</a> beach. Known as Cleat\'s Shore, it has been described as one of the quietest nudist facilities in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_industries">Other industries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Other industries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Farming and forestry are other important industries. Plans for 2008 for a large <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Salmon" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic Salmon">salmon</a> farm holding 800,000 or more fish in Lamlash Bay have been criticised by the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Arran_Seabed_Trust" title="Community of Arran Seabed Trust">Community of Arran Seabed Trust</a>. They fear the facility could jeopardise Scotland\'s first marine No Take Zone, which was announced in September 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arran_logo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6d/Arran_logo.png/220px-Arran_logo.png" width="220" height="107" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/6/6d/Arran_logo.png 1.5x" data-file-width="240" data-file-height="117" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arran_logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Brewery logo</div></div></div>\n<p>The Arran Brewery is a <a href="/wiki/Microbrewery" title="Microbrewery">microbrewery</a> founded in March 2000 in <a href="/wiki/Cladach" title="Cladach">Cladach</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Brodick" title="Brodick">Brodick</a>. It makes eight regular <a href="/wiki/Cask_ale" title="Cask ale">cask</a> and <a href="/wiki/Filtered_beer" title="Filtered beer">bottled</a> beers. The wheat beer, Arran Blonde (5.0% <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_by_volume" title="Alcohol by volume">abv</a>) is the most popular; others include Arran Dark and Arran Sunset,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> with a seasonal Fireside Ale brewed in winter. The brewery is open for tours and tastings.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The business went into liquidation in May 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> but was then sold to Marketing Management Services International Ltd in June 2008. It is now back in production and the beers widely available in Scotland, including certain Aldi stores. However, there were redundancies in 2017 and again in 2018. <sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Other businesses include Arran Aromatics, which produces a range of luxury toiletries, perfumes and candles, Arran Dairies, Arran Cheese Shop, James\'s Chocolates and Wooleys of Arran.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Scottish Gaelic dialect of Arran died out when the last speaker Donald Craig died in the 1970s. However, there is now a Gaelic House in Brodick, set up at the end of the 1990s. <a href="/wiki/Brodick_Castle" title="Brodick Castle">Brodick Castle</a> features on the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bank_of_Scotland" title="Royal Bank of Scotland">Royal Bank of Scotland</a> \xc2\xa320 note and <a href="/wiki/Lochranza_Castle" title="Lochranza Castle">Lochranza Castle</a> was used as the model for the castle in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Adventures_of_Tintin" title="The Adventures of Tintin">The Adventures of Tintin</a></i> adventure <i><a href="/wiki/The_Black_Island" title="The Black Island">The Black Island</a></i>.\n</p><p>Arran has one newspaper, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Arran_Banner" title="The Arran Banner">The Arran Banner</a></i>. It was listed in the <i>Guinness Book of Records</i> in November 1984 as the "local newspaper which achieves the closest to a saturation circulation in its area." The entry reads: "<i>The Arran Banner</i>, founded in 1974, has a readership of more than 97 per cent in Britain\'s seventh largest off-shore island."<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> There is also an online monthly publication called <i>Voice for Arran</i>, which mainly publishes articles contributed by community members.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2010 an "Isle of Arran" version of the game <a href="/wiki/Monopoly_(game)" title="Monopoly (game)">Monopoly</a> was launched.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Knitting" title="Knitting">knitting</a> style used to create <a href="/wiki/Aran_sweater" class="mw-redirect" title="Aran sweater">Aran sweaters</a> is often mistakenly associated with the Isle of Arran rather than the Irish <a href="/wiki/Aran_Islands" title="Aran Islands">Aran Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Nature_and_conservation">Nature and conservation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Nature and conservation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sorbus_arranensis.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Sorbus_arranensis.JPG/220px-Sorbus_arranensis.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Sorbus_arranensis.JPG/330px-Sorbus_arranensis.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Sorbus_arranensis.JPG/440px-Sorbus_arranensis.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2288" data-file-height="1712" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sorbus_arranensis.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Sorbus_arranensis" title="Sorbus arranensis">Sorbus arranensis</a></i> in flower at <a href="/wiki/Eglinton_Country_Park" title="Eglinton Country Park">Eglinton Country Park</a>, Irvine.</div></div></div>\n<p>The island has three <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> species of tree, the <a href="/wiki/Arran_whitebeams" title="Arran whitebeams">Arran whitebeams</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Scotsman_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scotsman-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> These trees are the Scottish or Arran whitebeam (<i><a href="/wiki/Sorbus_arranensis" title="Sorbus arranensis">Sorbus arranensis</a></i>), the bastard mountain ash or cut-leaved whitebeam (<i><a href="/wiki/Sorbus_pseudofennica" title="Sorbus pseudofennica">Sorbus pseudofennica</a></i>)<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> and the Catacol whitebeam (<i><a href="/wiki/Sorbus_pseudomeinichii" title="Sorbus pseudomeinichii">Sorbus pseudomeinichii</a></i>). If rarity is measured by numbers alone they are amongst the most endangered tree species in the world. They are protected in Glen Diomhan off <a href="/wiki/Catacol" title="Catacol">Glen Catacol</a>, at the north end of the island by a partly fenced off <a href="/wiki/National_nature_reserve_(United_Kingdom)" title="National nature reserve (United Kingdom)">national nature reserve</a>, and are monitored by staff from <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Natural_Heritage" title="Scottish Natural Heritage">Scottish Natural Heritage</a>. Only 236 <i>Sorbus pseudofennica</i> and 283 <i>Sorbus arranensis</i> were recorded as mature trees in 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-Bignal_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bignal-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> They are typically trees of the mountain slopes, close to the tree line. However, they will grow at lower altitudes, and are being preserved within Brodick Country Park.\n</p><p>Over 200 species of bird have been recorded on Arran including <a href="/wiki/Black_guillemot" title="Black guillemot">black guillemot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_eider" title="Common eider">eider</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peregrine_falcon" title="Peregrine falcon">peregrine falcon</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Golden_eagle" title="Golden eagle">golden eagle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wild_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wild-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> In 1981 there were 28 <a href="/wiki/Rock_ptarmigan" title="Rock ptarmigan">ptarmigan</a> on Arran, but in 2009 it was reported that extensive surveys had been unable to record any.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>  Similarly, the <a href="/wiki/Red-billed_chough" title="Red-billed chough">red-billed chough</a> no longer breeds on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> 108&#160;km<sup>2</sup> of Arran\'s upland areas is designated a <a href="/wiki/Special_Protection_Area" title="Special Protection Area">Special Protection Area</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Natura_2000" title="Natura 2000">Natura 2000</a> programme due to its importance for breeding <a href="/wiki/Hen_harriers" class="mw-redirect" title="Hen harriers">hen harriers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Red_deer" title="Red deer">Red deer</a> are numerous on the northern hills, and there are populations of <a href="/wiki/Red_squirrel" title="Red squirrel">red squirrel</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_badger" title="European badger">badger</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_otter" class="mw-redirect" title="European otter">otter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vipera_berus" title="Vipera berus">adder</a> and <a href="/wiki/Viviparous_lizard" title="Viviparous lizard">common lizard</a>. Offshore there are <a href="/wiki/Harbour_porpoise" title="Harbour porpoise">harbour porpoises</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basking_shark" title="Basking shark">basking sharks</a> and various species of <a href="/wiki/Dolphin" title="Dolphin">dolphin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wild_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wild-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The north of Lamlash Bay became a Marine Protected Area and No Take Zone under the <a href="/wiki/Marine_(Scotland)_Act_2010" title="Marine (Scotland) Act 2010">Marine (Scotland) Act 2010</a>, which means no fish or shellfish may be taken in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> In 2014 the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Government" title="Scottish Government">Scottish Government</a> created Scotland\'s first <a href="/w/index.php?title=Marine_Conservation_Order&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Marine Conservation Order (page does not exist)">Marine Conservation Order</a> in order to protect delicate <a href="/wiki/Maerl" title="Maerl">maerl</a> beds off south Arran after fishermen breached a voluntary agreement not to <a href="/wiki/Trawling" title="Trawling">trawl</a> in the vicinity.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Arran_National_Scenic_Area">North Arran National Scenic Area</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: North Arran National Scenic Area">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width: -moz-min-content; width: -webkit-min-content; width: min-content; max-width: 100%;"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow: auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arran%27s_northern_hills_from_Ardrossan_ferry.jpg" class="image" title="Arran&#39;s Northern hills, viewed from the Ardrossan ferry, with Goat Fell the tallest peak."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Arran%27s_northern_hills_from_Ardrossan_ferry.jpg/1082px-Arran%27s_northern_hills_from_Ardrossan_ferry.jpg" width="1082" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Arran%27s_northern_hills_from_Ardrossan_ferry.jpg/1623px-Arran%27s_northern_hills_from_Ardrossan_ferry.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Arran%27s_northern_hills_from_Ardrossan_ferry.jpg/2164px-Arran%27s_northern_hills_from_Ardrossan_ferry.jpg 2x" data-file-width="16120" data-file-height="2235" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arran%27s_northern_hills_from_Ardrossan_ferry.jpg" title="File:Arran&#39;s northern hills from Ardrossan ferry.jpg"> </a></div>Arran\'s Northern hills, viewed from the Ardrossan ferry, with <a href="/wiki/Goat_Fell" title="Goat Fell">Goat Fell</a> the tallest peak.</div></div></div>\n<p>The northern part of the island is designated a <a href="/wiki/National_scenic_area_(Scotland)" title="National scenic area (Scotland)">national scenic area</a> (NSA),<sup id="cite_ref-nsa-map_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nsa-map-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> one of 40 such areas in Scotland which are defined so as to identify areas of exceptional scenery and to ensure its protection by restricting certain forms of development.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The North Arran NSA covers 27,304&#160;<a href="/wiki/Hectares" class="mw-redirect" title="Hectares">ha</a> in total, consisting of 20,360&#160;ha of land and a further 6,943&#160;ha of the surrounding sea.<sup id="cite_ref-area_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-area-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> It covers all of the island north of <a href="/wiki/Brodick" title="Brodick">Brodick</a> and <a href="/wiki/Machrie" title="Machrie">Machrie</a> Bay, as well as the main group of hills surrounding <a href="/wiki/Goat_Fell" title="Goat Fell">Goat Fell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nsa-map_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nsa-map-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_residents">Notable residents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Arran&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Notable residents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Calman" title="Kenneth Calman">Sir Kenneth Calman</a> (born 1941) \xe2\x80\x93 Chancellor of <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow University">Glasgow University</a>, former Scottish and UK Chief Medical Officer and author of the <a href="/wiki/Calman_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="Calman Commission">Calman Commission</a> on Scottish devolution<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Flora_Drummond" title="Flora Drummond">Flora Drummond</a> (1878\xe2\x80\x931949) \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Suffrage" title="Suffrage">suffragette</a></li>\n<li>Lieut. Col. <a href="/wiki/James_Fullarton" title="James Fullarton">James Fullarton</a>, C. B., K. H. (1782\xe2\x80\x931834) \xe2\x80\x93 fought at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Waterloo" title="Battle of Waterloo">Battle of Waterloo</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Daniel_Macmillan" class="mw-redirect" title="Daniel Macmillan">Daniel Macmillan</a> (1813\xe2\x80\x931857) \xe2\x80\x93 He and his brother <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Macmillan_(publisher)" class="mw-redirect" title="Alexander Macmillan (publisher)">Alexander</a> founded <a href="/wiki/Macmillan_Publishers" title="Macmillan Publishers">Macmillan Publishers</a> in 1843. His grandson was <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Harold_Macmillan" title="Harold Macmillan">Harold Macmillan</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jack_McConnell" title="Jack McConnell">Jack McConnell</a> (born 1960) \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/First_Minister_of_Scotland" title="First Minister of Scotland">First Minister of Scotland</a> (2001\xe2\x80\x932007)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_McLellan" title="Robert McLellan">Robert McLellan</a> (1907\xe2\x80\x931985) \xe2\x80\x93 playwright and poet in <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Alison_Prince" title="Alison Prince">Alison Prince</a> (born 1931) \xe2\x80\x93 children\'s writer</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/J._M._Robertson" title="J. M. Robertson">J. M. Robertson</a> (1856\xe2\x80\x931933) \xe2\x80\x93 politician and journalist</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
